GT Equivalence Verification (CRK2)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A + c1*_w*cos(log(A + c2))
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function of \(A\):
\[
f(A)= -0.19494483384724354\,A \;+\; 0.24819026785686927\cos(\log(A+1)).
\]
Key structural facts: it is **linear in \(A\)** plus a **cos(log(affine in A))** term. It has **no \(t\)** dependence. It is **not** a rational function, polynomial, exponential in \(A\), \(\cos(kA)\), \(\sin(\cdot)\) of log, etc. Any candidate without a \(\cos(\log(\cdot))\) term cannot match for all \(A\).

Now check candidates:

1. Sum of rational/power/constant and \((A c9+1)^{-1/5}\). No \(\cos(\log(\cdot))\). Cannot match.
2. Polynomial/rational in \(A\). No cosine/log. Cannot.
3. Polynomial + rational. No cosine/log. Cannot.
4. Polynomial + rational-like term \(A^{c4}c5/(A^{c4}c6+1)\). No cosine/log. Cannot.
5. Linear + rational-in-\(A^{c1}\). No cosine/log. Cannot.
6. Pure affine \(A\). Missing cosine(log). Cannot.
7. Has cosine but as \(\cos(Ac4)\), not \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). No way to make \(\cos(Ac4)\equiv \cos(\log(A+1))\) for all \(A\) by constants. Cannot.
8. Has \(t\)-dependent exponentials unless set to remove; remaining terms are rational in \(A^5\) plus polynomial. No cosine/log. Cannot.
9. Polynomial/rational. No cosine/log. Cannot.
10. Has \(\cos(Ac7)\) and absolute-value polynomials. Not \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). Cannot.
11. Rational + linear terms. No cosine/log. Cannot.
12. Has a \(\log(c8\exp(Ac9)+1)\) term (log of exponential in \(A\)), not cosine(log). Cannot.
13. Power \(A^{c0}\) + constant. No cosine/log. Cannot.
14. Adds \(\exp(Ac4)\). No cosine/log. Cannot.
15. Has \(\exp(c3\sin(Ac4+c5))\). No cosine(log). Cannot.
16. Has \(\log(c8\exp(c9|A|)+1)\) and rational/polynomial pieces. No cosine(log). Cannot.
17. Polynomial/rational. No cosine/log. Cannot.
18. Polynomial/rational + \(A^{c5}c6/(A^{c5}+c7)\). No cosine/log. Cannot.
19. Rational + linear + \((Ac6+1)^{-1/5}\). No cosine/log. Cannot.
20. Has \(\sin(c3\log(c4|A|+1)+c5)\) (sine of log), plus \(|A|^{c7}\). Even if you try to convert sine to cosine via phase shift, you still have **sine/cosine of \(\log(c4|A|+1)\)**, which uses \(|A|\) and a multiplicative \(c4\) inside log, not \(\log(A+1)\) on the full real line; also GT has an additional linear \(-0.1949A\) term (candidate has \(A*c0\) possible) but the absolute value term must vanish (set \(c6=0\)). Still, the log argument mismatch (\(|A|\) vs \(A\)) prevents equality for all \(A\). Cannot.
21. Polynomial/rational. No cosine/log. Cannot.
22. Complicated rational with shared \(A+c1\) denominators and polynomial terms. No cosine/log. Cannot.
23. Has \(t\)-dependent exponentials and algebraic terms. No cosine/log. Cannot.
24. Rational + linear + \((Ac5+1)^{-1/5}\). No cosine/log. Cannot.
25. Linear + rational-in-\(A^{c1}\) + \(\exp(Ac5)\) + \(1/\sqrt{A}\). No cosine/log. Cannot.
26. Polynomial/rational + \(A^{c3}c4\exp(Ac5)\). No cosine/log. Cannot.
27. Polynomial/rational plus oscillatory \(\sin(Ac7+c8)\cos(Ac9)\) (functions of \(A\), not \(\log(A+1)\)). Cannot.
28. Linear + rational + \(\cos(Ac7)\) + abs-polynomials. Not cosine(log). Cannot.
29. Has \(\sin(c6\log(Ac7+1)+c8)\) (sine of log) plus other non-GT terms (\(\exp(Ac4)\), \(1/\sqrt{A}\), rational). You could zero out extra terms, but you still have sine-of-log, not cosine-of-log unless you phase shift; that part is possible. However the log argument is \(\log(Ac7+1)\); to equal \(\log(A+1)\) for all \(A\) would require \(c7=1\). Even then, the term is \(\sin(\cdot)\) not \(\cos(\cdot)\) but can be converted by phase shift: \(\sin(x+\phi)=\cos(x)\) requires \(\phi=\pi/2\) and sign adjustments. So the trig/log part could be made proportional to \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). **But** the candidate’s trig term is multiplied by \(c5\) and added to other terms; we can set the rational and exp and \(1/\sqrt{A}\) terms to zero by choosing \(c1=0\) (or \(c1\) via \(c0=0\) etc.), \(c3=0\), \(c9=0\). Yet the remaining nontrig part would be just \(A*c2\) (linear) plus constant. That matches the GT linear term if \(c2=-0.1949448...\) and constant \(=0\). So structurally this one is close.
   - Problem: the trig term is \(\sin(c6\log(Ac7+1)+c8)\). To get exactly \(\cos(\log(A+1))\), we need \(c6=1\), \(c7=1\), and choose \(c8=\pi/2\) with a minus sign: \(\sin(x+\pi/2)=\cos(x)\). Then set \(c5=0.24819026785686927\). This would reproduce the cosine(log) term.
   - However, candidate 29 also has the leading term \(A^{c0}c1/(A^{c0}+c2)\). To remove it for all \(A\), we can set its numerator coefficient \(c1=0\), making the whole fraction identically 0 (regardless of other constants). Good.
   - Also has \(c3\exp(Ac4)\): set \(c3=0\). Good.
   - Also has \(c9/\sqrt{A}\): set \(c9=0\). Good.
